SENATOR SHORTRIDGE
ADMITTED TO THE BAR
Been Set Afire by
Tramps.
Fire broke out in an unoccupied dwell
ing house in the rear of 1410 Fol-som
street last" night and for a time a serious
blaze was imminent. Alarms were turned
in from boxes 78 and 79 and the Fire De
partment was promptly on the scene and
prevented the spread of the flames. The
fire was haTd to get at, owing to blind
alleys and the closeness of the adjoining
buildings. Before the flames were got un
der control the Swedish Baptist Church
on Tenth street was in flames. The in
terior of the sacred edifice was flooded
with water and was damaged by the
flames. For a time St. Joseph's Church
was in danger.
According to James Murphy, who owns
the house that was destroyed, the place
was unoccupied. He states that his fam
ily had retired and he was awakened
from a sound sleep by his neighbor's
warnings. He believes some tramps set
fire to the house. The structure was in
sured. ... _
A newly erected house owned by Dr.
Stealey was partly damaged by the
flames. The household-belongings of Mrs.
Swi.ns.on and C. R. Gardilious were dam
aged by smoke and water. Mr. Gardilious
had just moved in and intended taking
his bride, whom he marries to-morrow, to
his new home. He says he was not in
sured. _ . ..
When the alarm of fire was given the
Teamsters' Union was holding a meeting
in Teutonia Hall, a block away. Some
member said J. B. Cole's stable was on
fire, and in a few seconds a motion to ad
journ was made and carried. The mem
bers rushed to the fire, and on finding
that the stable was safe proceeded to
save the church property. The teamsters
carried out organs, desks, tables and oth
er paraphernalia in quick time, and it is
due to their presence that the loss to the
Swedish Baptist Church will be lessened.

Suggestions have been advanced that
the organization could add largely to its
strength of membership If assurance were
given that certain aspirants for office
would receive the support of the league
5n the municipal nominating convention.
The directors have positively refused to
entertain such propositions. The object
of the newly incorporated association Is
to give anti-boss Republicans a common
rallying point, so that good government
may be obtained through harmonious Re
publican agency.

. OF ALL KERN COUNTY
OAKLAND. June 13,-The exclusive
society circles of Oakland were
given an Interesting bit of news
to-day in the announcement of
the engagement of George Whea
ton and Miss Ida Belle Palmer. Mr.
Wheaton is the only son of Mr. and Mrs.
George H. Wheaton of Lakeside and a
brother of Mrs. Edson F. Adams. Miss
Palmer is the eldest daughter of Mr. and
Mrs. Charles E. Palmer, her father being
cashier of the Union National Bank. The
young lady is one of Oakland's most
beautiful women, with a stately carriage
and of a pronounced blonde type.
The two families have been among the
leaders in the, social life of the city. For
years the Wheaton home has been nota
ble as the center of much entertainment,
Mrs. Wheaton being considered peerless
as a hostess.
Mr. Wheaton is a leading member of
the Athenian Club of Oakland and of the
Bohemian Club of San Francisco. His
business relations have been as promi
nently successful as his social life and
friends galore will hasten to tender their
warmest congratulations to the prospec
tive benedict.
M!s.s Palmer's social debut was made at
the Wedding of Colonel -Oscar Fltzalan
Long and Miss Amy Requa, which she
attended as a bridesmaid. The young de
butante attracted marked attention be
cause of her beauty and she has been
considered as one of the remarkably
handsome girls of the city. " .
1 Since her' debut Miss Palmer has been
much sought at society functions. She
was a leader in the fashionable cotillons
BONES OF MISSIONARIES
DISCOVERED BY SOU3IERS
Remains of the Men Captured and
Eaten by Cannibals in New
Guinea Found.
VICTORIA, B. C, June 13.â The story
of the massacre of the Rev. James Chal
mers, Prof. Tomkins and fourteen native
teachers at the mouth of the Aird River,
in New Guinea, by cannibals, ( was
brought by the steamer Miowera. \ The
missionaries had gone on the schooner
Niue to Aird River, and on the arrival of
tht> schooner 100 canoes came alongside,
their occupants being all armed with
bows, arrows, spears and clubs. Despite
the warlike appearance of the natives the
missionaries landed, and after their boat
turned around a small mango clump they
were not seen again from the schooner.
A force of Australian artillery was sent
to investigate, and on their arrival were
attacked by the natives, whom they drove
oft and followed into the bush, taking and
destroying ten villages. Some of the prls r
oneis taken stated that when the mission
aries left their schooner they were taken
up a creek and surrounded by. a party of
natives. Chalmers was caught by the
arm and dragged toward the village,
which was within fifty yards. He was
then clubbed and his head was cut off
with bamboo knives in sight of Tomkins
and other members of the party. Chal
mers' body was cut and eaten the same
day. Tomkins was kept till the next day.
After Tomkins had been killed the mem
bers of the native mission crew were
killed and their flesh was distributed
among ten villages. The scene where
Chalmers was eaten was found, together
with parts of clothing, a jawbone with
teeth and some thigh bones.

PLAGUEININDIA
In the Patna IM vision of Bengal the
Cases Beach a Total of
437,681.
WASHINGTON. June 13.â The fearful
ravages of plague in British East India
are increasing. In the Presidency of
Bombay during the week ended April 12
there were 1947 new cases and 1632 deaths.
This is an increase, of 172. cases and 127
deaths 'over the previous week. The in
crease is notable In Karachi, where 230
fresh plague cases and 209 deaths occurred.
In the same week 715 deaths were reported
and 432 others suspected in Bombay city.
There are many- thousands of plague
deaths reported from other provinces of
India, the largest number being in the
Patna division of Bengal, where, up to
April 27, the total of 437,681 cases were re
ported. .

The church in all ases has been inclined to
limit the family of God and especially to be
lieve that no new children could be born into
it. Narrow-minded members of every sect
have been inclined to consign all besides them
selves- to the uncovenanted mercies of God.
They have often prided themselves on their
hoarlness and antiquity and they have looked
askance upon a new organization as an in.
terloper that had no right to gather around
the family table. It 'was bo with the Sunday
school,' It waÂ» so especially with the Young
Men's Christian Association, but by llfty years
of faithful work in thousands of communities
It has proved its divine origin and Its right
to be counted In the family ot God. The Young
Men's Christian Association is the church at
work for young men, not this church or that.

CHINAMAN SHOT
IN ROSS ALLEY
Highbinder Puts Two
Bullets Through a
â¢ Fisherman.
Weapon Found in St. Louis
Alley, Through Which
Murderer Escapes.
- Tou Sing, a Chinese fisherman, was shot
and Instantly killed last ntsht while stand
ing in the doorway at 9 Ross alley. Two
shots were fired by the murderer, both
bullets passing through the body of Tou.
The murderer, after committing the
deed, turned and ran up St. Louis alley
and disappeared. The weapon with which
he did the shooting was found at the
head of the alley. : It was the regulation
highbinder revolver, long barreled and of
38 caliber.
The murderer was seen running from
the scene of his crime by a number of
Chinese lounging about the locality. They
made no effort to prevent his escape, and
when questioned later by the police offi
cers displayed their usual stolid taciturn
ity.
The murdered man was not very well
known in the Chinese quarter. Inquiries
as to his Identity led to the disclosure oC
nothing but his name and occupation.
The cause of the shooting is a mystery.
Police officers have no knowledge of
â¢which tong-. If any. You Sing belonged to
and are at a loss to account for tha
crime. :

West Baden Springs Hotel Is De
stroyed and Guests May Have
Perished.
INDIANAPOLIS, Ind., June 14.âTele
phone messages from Salem, Ind., to tha
Journal at 4 o'clock this morning say the
West Baden Springs Hotel at West Ba
den, Ind., has been destroyed by fire.
Great confusion prevails, and at this time
it cannot be stated whether the fire, waa
attended by loss of life. The hotel is the
largest hostelry in Indiana, having some
TOO or'SOO rooms, and cost a million dol
lars. The Insurance will amount to about
$100,000.

Wedding of a Sonoma Pastor.
SONOMA, June 13.â At the Methodist
Epicopal church In Oakdale a pretty wed
ding occurred Tuesday evening-, i when
the Rev. C. L. Peterson, pastor of the
Methodist church at Sonoma, was united
In marriage to Miss Lulu Lindsey, for the
past three years principal of the public
school at Tesla. Both young people are
well known and popular. The groom has
just completed a four years' course at the
University of the Pacific, and has during
the few months of his pastorate in Sono
ma succeeded In materially advancing 1
the Interests of his church. Dr. McClish,
president of the University of the Pa
cific, performed the ceremony. F. Mltch
eltree, editor of the Sonoma Valley Ex
positor, was best man. Miss Annie E.
Lindsey was- maid of honor. After the
ceremony a wedding supper was served.

justice of the Peace- Joachimsen gave
judgment yesterday for $200 In" favor of
U. Wrinkle; assignee of Kredo & i: Co.,'
who sued F. Sol for breaking a contract
to sell his lodging-house at 120 Ellis street.
Sol entered, into an ; agreement with tlie
firm to sell : the lodging-house for $2400/ A
condition of the agreement was that' if
It was sold through any other parties 1200
commission was to be paid to â¢ Kredo &
Co. Just the same. .The- house was. sold
through other.. parties and. Sol set up as a
defense that his signature to the contract
was a forgery- Theodore Kytka,' the writ
ing " expert, was' put on the stand and
after comparing Sol's signature with his
other handwriting testified that Sol had
signed the document. ....-- ; -.-Â¦.".. -

Redwood City Launched.
The hew 'steamship Redwood City .was
launched at 8'o'clock la^t evening by John
W. Dickie at his ship yard on Alameda
Point. The vessel was christened by. Miss
Hazel Mills, daughter * of J. E. Mills of
the Belllngham Bay Improvement Com
pany. -Captain -Henry Weber will have
command of the Redwood City, which will
be put in commission for coastwise trade.

EVENTS IN SOCIETY
The Fourth' of July committee met last
night In the Mayor's office and outlined
a general plan for the celebration of In
dependence day. It was decided to have
a parade In the morning; literary exer
cises and a regatta in the afternoon and
fireworks In the evAiing.
There will be no collection of funds this
year. The j finance committee recom
mended the following apportionment of
the $2500 allowed by the city:
Parade committee, $SCO: fireworks commit
tee,. $800; printing committee. $35; literary com
mittee, J150; press committee, $160; regatta
committee, $200; miscellaneous, $200.
It was agreed to have all the exercises
in -the open air. The regatta will com
prise races bet-ween launches, yachts and
rowboats.- The United States marines
willbe asked to join in the contests. G.
P. Pond and W. T. Hess resigned from
the committee , and- thÂ© Mayor .will ap
point their successors. Chairman Geist
ing announced the appointment of the
following committees, the first named of
each being chairman: : .

Cpmplaint Charging Him
With Perjury Will i Be
Piled To- Day. v;
The jury in the case, of "Sir" Harry
Westwood Cooper* alias Ernest Moore
Chadwlck,' charged with forgery in send
ing a forged telegram to Miss Norine
Schneider, after being out all night, came
into Judge Cook's court yesterday morn
ing and the foreman, H. K. Waterhou3e,
announced' that the members had been
unable to .agree upon a verdict. The
Judge asked. whether it was a matter of
fact. or- of law and the foreman replied
that it was on a matter of fact as to
whether the telegram had been sent, with
intent to defraud. The Judge said hÂ«
could not advise them and discharged
them. The case was then: set for to-mor
row, when it will be reset for the second
trial. The jury on the first ballot stoou
6 to 6. A second ballot stood 7 for convic
tion and 5 for acquittal and no change was
made.
After the jury was discharged Attorney
Murphy for the defendant asked the court
to order Mrs. . Schneider and her two
daughters into custody on the charge of
perjury. He declared that they perjured
themselves by testifying that no engage
ment existed between the defendant and
Miss Norine Schneider. T\.e Judge replied
that the fact of the engaeement was not a
material point In the case and declined to
take any action.
District Attorney Byington will file the
complaint charging Cooper with perjury,
as instructed by the Judge, to-day. The
charge is based upon the testimony of
Cooper that he had a private conversation
with Miss Norine Schneider on the even
ing of February 22, when it was arranged
between them that he should send her the
forged .telegram. That'. Is a material
point in the case.
Stands Seven for Convic
tion and Five for
. ' Acquittal. -
JURY IN COOPER
CASE DISAGREES
Owingf-to the fact that the overcrowded
detention shed at the Mall dock is. not in
good sanitary, condition, ; Collector Strat
ton released Su Shih Chin on. cash bail
given .by his custodians, the Pacific Mail
Steamship Company, last Wednesday, and
the : Chinese reformer, has comfortable
quarters among his own people. â¢ v â¢
He appeared before the Collector yester
day "to show cause why he should not be
deported. | The Dowager , Empress v.', of
China was represented -by her Imperial
Majesty's Consul General, Ho Yow. .Con
sul Ho objected to the admission: to. this'
country of Su on two grounds. , First, that
his section 6 certificate, describing him as
a traveler, had been obtained from a repre
sentative of the Chinese Government '.by
fraud and misrepresentation, and -second
that the paper was informal because there
was an unfilled blank in it. ' '-Â¦'Â¦' .
The transcript of 'the proceedings -r-wlll
be mailed to the Secretary of the Treas
ury as soon as prepared and Su will be de
tained here until the; Secretary passes
upon the case. .
The friends of Su are sanguine as to the
result. They say that if the worst hap
pens and Su should be deported to' Shang
hai, whence he came, he will be under the
protection of the British flag and can ob
tain, a Â¦ certificate Â¦ from â¢ the registrar., at
that port, which will entitle him to land
here. â¢ Â¦â¢'â¢'- Â¦.;-.,Â¦
Several hundred red circulars/in Chinese
characters were circulated in Chinatown
yesterday afternoon announcing that Su
would speak to the Chinese people of this
city in the Washington-street theater at
7 o'clock in the evening on the subject,
"Past, Present and Future of China."
Ho Tow will file a copy and translation
of the circular to-day with the Collector
-as an evidence that Mr. Su is not a
tralever, but a lecturer. < .- Â¦ ' ..

PLAYING WITH MATCHES
CAUSES CHILD'S DEATH
Mary Fitzpatrick^" Receives Fatal
Burns and Mother, Injured in \
. Trying to Save Her.
Mary. Fltzpatrlck. the four-year-old
child of William Fitzpatrick, a street car
conductor, received fatal injuries yester
day afternoon as the result of playing
with matches In the yard of her father' 3
residence, 54 Valley street. ; ,
The little girl secured a boz of matches
and amused herself by lighting them. A
pile of oil saturated rags was thus set
on fire and. the flames spread to the child's
clothing. - The screams, of the little girl
brought - her mother to the spot, ana in,
tryingto put out the flames Mrs/ Fitz
patrick was severely burned on the hands
and arms. : Dr. Hughes was oalled in to
attend the unfortunate child, and she was
removed ; to St. Luke's Hospital, where
siiG died- 1 last evenine. .- ~ .- _
OHIO SOCIETY LOSES
MEMBER IN LYNCHING
Resolution Passed .Condemning^ in
Strong Terms Outrage Committed
' . by Modoc County Mob.
The Ohio Society passed the following
resolution at its meeting Wednesday
nieht:
Whereas, We learn thruogh the public press
that a native of Ohio, named Calvin Hall, en
rolled in our recent roster as a resident , of
Lookout, Modoc County, was hanged by. a mob
on May 31, 1901; therefore, be it
ResSlved, That ? we i condemn the :Â¦ cowardly
miscreants who perpetrated this dastardly deed,
â¢nd that we call upon all Ohloans and other
law-abiding citizens of i Mcdoc County to lend
ahand to the State and county authorities in
ferreting out .the murderers and to assist in
bringing them to Justice.'. ~i Â¦ Â¦'Â¦ ,~,
PILOT JORDAN SUED
FOR A LARGE SUM
Sixty-Five Thousand Dollars Asked
for the Death of Two of
Rio's Crew. x . .
Catherine Brady, widow of Second As
sistant Engineer Thomas H. Brady, who
was drowned on the occasion of the wreck
of the Rio de Janeiro on the 22d of last
February, filed suit In the United States
District Court yesterday against Freder
ick. W. Jordan and nineteen other pilots
to recover $15,000 damages for the loss of
her husband. .
The complaint alleges that the wreck of
the Rio was caused by the. negligence and
unskillfulness of Pilot Jordan, who was
in i exclusive command of the vessel at
the time she struck. , Her four children
are parties plaintiff to the suit.
A similar suit for $50,000 damages for
the death of Water Tender J. H. Smith
was filed against the same defendants by
the family of the dead man. It is alleged
that all the defendants are partners.
COUNTEKFEIT DIE IS
RENDERED HARMLESS
George T. McDonnell's Counsel Ar
gues That tho Government Failed
' . to Present a Case.
George T. McDonnell was placed on
trial yesterday in the United. States Did
trlct Court before Judge do Huven and a
Jury. Duncan K. McKlnlay. Assistant
United States District Attorney, appeared
for the Government and Bert Schlesinger
for the defendant.
The testimony was to tho effect that
McDonnell. Chimes Koenlg and Dewltt
E. Young procured to be made a steel die
for the coining of one-dollar pieces. The
impression, however, did not seem to be
a success, for it was filed off before any
money was stamped and the die remained
blank. Mr. Schlesinger argued that ths
die being blank there was no case against
his client. Mr. McKinlay tookithe ground
that a complete die had been made and
that the offense for which McDonnell had
been Indicted had been committed, and
that the subsequent erasure by filing did
not relieve the offender of culpability.
The case will be given to the Jury this
morning.
The preliminary examination of Charles
Kewitz. charged with making a die for
counterfeiting money, was held yesterday
before United States Court Commissioner
Heacock. Thomas D. Riordan, counsel for
the defendant, raised tho point that as
only half a die was found by the officers
Kewitz had not committed the offense of
making a. die. This case went over until
to-day to allow Mr. Riordan an opportu
nity of producing authorities.
President Charles M. Hays of the
Southern Pacific and General Manager
Kruttschnitt are racing to New York.
Why they are in such a hurry to reach
the Eastern metropolis is a question as
yet unsolved by those in the yellow build
ing. . "
When they left here on Monday even
ing Hays and Kruttschnitt each had his
private car attached to the train. It was
first planed that Kruttschnitt should
travel only as far as Ogden and then re
turn to San Francisco, inspecting the road
on his way. The plans were changed,
however, and when the special arrived at
Ogden Kruttschnitt's car was uncoupled
from the train and was sent back to this
city, while the general manager boarded
the president's car and, sped on eastward.
' The special is rushing forward at top
speed, which causes old railroad men to
shake their heads and mutter, "There Is
something in, the wind."' Hays and
Kruttschnitt will hold a conference with
President Bert of the Union Pacific at
Omaha and will then journey on to New
York. . â¢ . ,
: A prominent railroad official, in speak
ing , of Hays' trip East, said yesterday
that on the return of the railroad presi
dent to this city there will be some big
changes in the Southern Pacific. He re
marked: Â¦ .
"I feel positive that the trip East is for
a conference between Hays and.Harrlman
in â¢ reference â¢ to â¢ curtailing expenses.-: -I
think that a closer consolidation will 1 be
made between the Union and Southern
Pacific^.roads. Take, for Instance the
land departments of the Southern Pacific
and 'Union Pacific. I would not- be the
least surprised to hear that the two offices
will be consolidated at once and the head
quarters-moved to Omaha, with a small
branch - maintained here." â¢ .'
J. C. Stubbs is still in New Tork and
there has been no indication of his re
turn to San Francisco. It is more than
possible that he will await the coming: of
Hays. *
. H. E. Fitzhugh has taken up his duties
as assistant to President Hays. He has
not been allotted an office in the railroad
building, but; his letters are delivered on
the executive floor, all his official letters
being addressed. "H. B. Fitzhusrh, Assist
ant to the President of the Southern Pa
cific." . .

A notice which was served on Auditor
"Wells yesterday by the attorneys of the
First. National Bank and John W. Mack
ay will result in tying up indefinitely the
surplus fund of the present year, which
has been apportioned b'y the Supervisors
to pay _ back claims of merchants, and
teachers against tho city. Tho notice is
in effect n protest against the proposed
intention to pny other creditors, whereas
no provision has been made in tho budget
to liquidate tho clnlms of the two protest
ants named, which claims have boon put
in final judgment.
The nmoiint? involved include a Judg
ment for $10,488 09 ngnlnat the city for
taxes paid under protest and since ad
judged to be Illegal, and three more Judg
ment claims of tho same character hold
by J. W.'i Mackay for, respectively,
$1284 84, $19,063 Co and $15,138 44. The notices
served on the Auditor are four in num
btr, one of which ls as follows: ,
We herewith present to you a transcript of
the docket of the final judgment given and
made by the Superior Court of the city and
county of San Francisco on the 11th day of
August, 1900, In the action then pending in said
court, numbered 54,339, and wherein John W.
Mackey et al., trustees, etc., were plaintiffs,
and the city and county of San Francisco was
defendant. â¢
And we hereby notify you that the principal
amount- of said judgment bears interest at the
rate of 7 per cent per annum from the date of
rendition until paid; and. we hereby demand
and require of you the allowance and payment
of the amount of Bald Jud&ment and interest'
thereon out of the "surplus fund" in the treas
ury of the city and county of San Francisco
for the fiscal year ending Juno 30, 1901; and you
are notified, requested and required to retain
at all times and until such allowance and pay
ment a sufficient amount of the moneys coming
and to come into said '"surplus fund" to pay
the said Judgment and the interest thereon as
aforesaid. - ' \ - .. Â¦ . Â¦ .. Â¦Â¦
Concerning the protests Auditor Wells
says that although the charater. specific

Protestants unless directed to. do -so. by.
the Board of ; Supervisors or by an- order
of court. The budget is now. in the hands
of the Mayor, who has informed the at
torneys for Mackay and the bank that no

THE Grand Circle of the Druld
esses, U. A. O. D. of California,
will hold its annual session in the
Sutter-street Druids' Temple on
Tuesday next. The authority to
institute the Grand Circle, the ladies'
branch of the United Ancient Order ,of
Druids, -vfas obtained last- year through
the efforts of Supreme Representative
WILL TIE UP
SURPLUS FUND
James F. MartinonI from the Supreme
Grove of the United States and was the
first charter issued to institute such a
body. The Grand Circle was organized
a few months ago and there are now nine
circles that owe allegiance to it. Three
more are ready to come in.
The present grand arch druidess, Mrs.
Thornhill, will retire from office and she
will be followed by Mrs. A. Sorensen of
Mistletoe Circle. Modesto, who will be
elected to the highest office for the term
of one year. .Miss Bessie Fabb-ri of El
Dorado Circle of this city, the grand sec
retary, will be a candidate for re-election,
and 'as her-.work : for the order and the
Grand' Circle 'has been satisfactory, it is
probable that- she will be continued in of
fice. There will be quite a number of
candidates for the other offices, but as
the members of the grand body are quite
new at the business of Grand Circle work
they have not yet made their selections
for the other positions.
Much work will be necessary during the
coming-year in the line of official visita
tions, arranging: for the establishment of
new circles; and their Institution and also
in the installation of new officers.
Army officers stationed in this city were
unanimous in expressing their indignation
yesterday of the alleged "army frauds"
developed by a "yellow" morning paper,
aided by an equally saffron-hued evening
contemporary.
Investigations made yesterday show
that in the entire city a little more than
$400 worth of soldiers' clothing and sup
pliea had been found in the second-hand
stores and pawn shops. Army officers are
of opinion that possibly a similar amount
of army clothing might have been hidden
away by some of the dealers, who became
alarmed at the fear of prosecution at the
hands of the Government.
In the last three years more than 75,000
soldiers have passed through this city,
either going to or returning from the
Philippines, and it has not been an un
common thing for the soldiers to sell or
pawn portions of their equipment.
, A number of pawnbrokers were prose
cuted at the outbreak of the war for hav
ing soldiers' clothing in their possession
and the recent presence of thousands of
fighting men led to a renewal of the
licit traffic in Uncle Sam's property.
â¢ Will Prosecute Dealers.
The fact that army shoes were adver
tised for sale by second-hand dealers In
this city led to a request being- made by
Inspector General Maus of General Shat
ter's staff that the United States District
Attorney, Marshall B. Woodworth, prose
cute the principal dealers in the goods.
,.The sensational morning newspaper that
published the story of "big army frauds"
was engaged at the same time in looking
for opium smokers in a low resort of the
city and evidently indulged in a "pipe
dream" at the expense of the reputation
oj the nation's gallant army.
After a search of all the second-hand
stores and pawnshops in the city, the In
spector general, aided by city detectives,
"rounded up" a quantity of Government
property and placed it In a warehouse.
The "yellow" papers, dazzled by the
prospect of securing for once a genuine
item of news, lost, their senses and dis
covered a "warehouse filled with stolen
clothing belonging to the army.".
The number of soldiers who have In the
last three years sold some of the cloth
ing Issued to them by the Government, as
compared to the total of the number quar
tered in San Francisco, is so small that It
would require decimal fractions to express
the percentage. - Â¦>
The "round-up" of Uncle Sam's prop
erty in the second-hand stores and pawn
shops this week shows that eleven
blankets were found, together with five
leggings, one blouse, forty-eight blue
flannel shirts, two gauntlets, seventy
eight pairs of black shoes and fifty-three
pairs of tan shoes.
Army Officers Indignant.
General Shatter was indignant yester
day on reading certain published state
ments reflecting on the honor of the of
ficers of the army in the Department of
California and his views were shared by
every -member of his staff.
Lieutenant Colonel M. P. Maus, Inspect
or general of the department, was em
phatic in denouncing the yellow publica
tions as an outrage.
Accused Dealers Silent.
"No charges have been filed against any
one in the army," he said, "and none will
be. No frauds have been committed, and
it is outrageous that the honor of the
army should be so grossly attacked.
Statements like those published will hurt
the city also. We knew that certain deal
ers were advertising Government clothing
and sought to bring the parties to justice.
No one in the army was accused, and we
did not know how these dealers came into
possession of the goods. We assumed that
the property had been sold by- some of
the soldiers while quartered In this city.
The traffic In clothing is Injurious to the
health and morale of the army, and it
will have to stop. From now on regular
search will be made for pawned clothing
belonging to the Government and it will
bo seized. This will serve to prevent the
dealers and pawnbrokers from doing busi
ness with the soldiers. Men have been
known to sell their supplies a few days
after receiving the same, and we could
not send the men "to the Philippines un
equipped. We had to replace the articles
they disposed of previous to their sailing
from this port."
Lipman Abrams and his son, George
Abrams, who were arrested on Tuesday
night for having soldiers' clothing and
supplies in their possession, were ques
tioned yesterday by the United States
District Attorney. The arrested men re
fused to give the names of the soldiers
from whom they had bought the goods
or give any Information In the matter
untll> they had consulted an attorney. Ike
Abrams is still at large and the police are
searching for htm. The bail of the ac
cused men has been fixed at $5000.
Captain A. W. Klmball, post quarter
master at the Presidio, denounced the
story of frauds In his department as a
pure fabrication. He stated that there
was no Irregularity in his department and
that a careful system of checking sup
plies prevented anything of the kind.
"The goods found in the pawnshops,"
said Captain Kimball, "were sold by dis
charged soldiers. AH clothing issued to
troops at the Presidio was from this of
fice. I have receipts of various officers
for clothing Issued to their regiments on
requisition, and these receipts, with the
balance of clothing on hand, tallies with
the amount received from. the depot quar
termaster." - : .
Colonel Rawles. commandant at the
Presidio/ characterized the stories of
army frauds as "perfect -rot." The of
ficer stated that it was well known that
the soldiers sold their clothing, and that
when evidence was secured steps had al
ways been taken to punish the seller and
the purchaser.
Colonel W. M. Wallace of the Fifteenth
Cavalry, stationed at the* Presidio, stated
that the stories of fraud were, absurd
He ridiculed the statements that gTeat
quantities of soldiers' clothing had been
purchased by secord-hand dealers.
Many officers at the Presidio and those
on duty ac army headquarters In the Phe
lan building also expressed themselves In
positive terms to the effect that the al
leged "army frauds" existed only in the
columns of sensational papers.
James K. Ross, an attorney of the local
bar, will be cited this morning by Judge
Kerrigan to appear and show cause why
he should not be punished for contempt of
court for having placed In' the hands of
his client, Thomas F. Kollman, what pur
ported to be a copy of a decree of'divlrce,
under the provisions of which Kollman
believed he was a "widower." Kollman.
was cited on the 11th inst, to appear this
morning before Judge Kerrigan and show
cause why he should not be punished for
contempt of court for failing to pay At
torney O. C. Pratt, who represents Mrs.
Kollman, counsel fees in the sum of $50
to enable Mrs. Kollman to prosecute her
cross complaint in the suit instituted by
"her husband.
Kollman's idea of a cross-complaint in
the case was hazy, and as he believed that
he had secured a decree of divorce and
had therefore divested his wife of the
right to "prosecute" he instituted an in
vestigation. The records in the office of
the County Clerk showed that no decree
had been issued in his case and that, fur
thermore, his default had been entered
to the cross-complaint tiled by his wife,
which bars him irom making further de
fense to her action.
The result was that Kollman plac'ed the
copy of the alleged decree of divorce pur
porting to free him from his wife in the
hands of Judge Kerrigan. The order di
recting him to' appear and show cause
why he should not be punished for con
tempt was also placed in the hands of the
court, together with a remarkable agree
ment that bears the signature of his at
torney, Ross. This agreement reads:
SAN FRANCISCO, April 23, 1901.
I hereby guarantee that on payment of the
full sum of $100 I will procure a divorce
for Thomas V. K/llman, and that there will be
no more trouble or no more money demanded
by me; that same shall be in full of all de
mands. JAS=. K. ROSS.
Acting upon these papers Judge Kerri
gan will call upon Ross to appear and
make his defense.
Regarding, the manner in which he had
been deceived, Kollman, who conducts a
barber shop on Pacific street, near Hyde,
said:
"I brought suit against my wife last
April, in which 1 asked for a decree of
divorpe on the grounds of cruelty and de
sertion. My attorney entered into the
agreement which is in the possession of
Judge Kerrigan and I paid him part of
the sum on account. 'The case was called
for hearing and I testified as to my wife's
desertion and cruel treatment of me. A
few days after the case was tried Attor
ney Ross called upon me to pay. the bal
ance due him and said that upon such
payment I would get my decree.
â¢ "I got my mother to advance me the
money and I paid the balance, for which
I- hold a receipt, and Attorney Ross gave
me a copy of the decree, which he said
had been issued in my favor, at the same
time saying. 'Now you are a widower.'
"I believed that I was divorced until a
few days ago, when I was served with the
copy of this order to show cause why I
should not be punished for contempt of
court. I went to see my lawyer. He said
that he had done all he had agreed to do
for me and refused to have anything fur
ther to do with the case. I was informed,
however, that if I would pay Attorney
Pratt, who represents my Â¦wife. Mrs. Mary
A. Kollman, the sum of $35 I would
not be bothered any more.
"Then I went again to see Attorney
Ross,, but he refused to do anything for
me. Attorney Pratt's clerk came often to
my house and said that if I did not 'put
up' I would be'sent to jail. I would do
anything in reason, but I have no money.
My shop is n one-chair shop and I only
make $6 or $7 a week. My mother has
also given me the money to pay Ross
with, find I do not care to get more from
her, as she is old and feeble and needs all
she has."
Judge Kerrigan's examination of Attor
ney lloss will only go Into his act in sup
plying Kollman with the fictitious "copy"
of a decree of divorce. It is doubtful'if
the court has the authority to question
the contract bearing Ross" signature,
though in tho agreement Ross binds him
self for a consideration to secure a de
cree which he did not secure and which
Judpe Kerrigan says was not issued be
cause the proofs were" insufficient. .
